    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_168163610" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168163610" />
    <a title="DJL" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5135799-djl"><img alt="DJL" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579210542p2/5135799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168163610?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DJL" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DJL" href="/user/show/5135799-djl">DJL</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5135799-djl?shelf=ya-literature">ya-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5135799-djl?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5135799-djl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168163610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12323232421948341848"><i>Originally posted on my blog, <a href='http://djlibrariandishes.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Denim-Jacket Librarian Dishes</a></i><br/><br/>Who wouldn't want to rid themselves of any and all sickness or heal any injury the moment after it happens? To be free from such pitfalls as getting winded while running or healing muscles to help them grow stronger. It would sound like a good deal to most people. But for those with such abilities, like Ada, it is as much the dark side of the coin as it is the light especially when others want that skill for themselves alone. No one shou</span>
  <span id="freeText12323232421948341848" style="display:none"><i>Originally posted on my blog, <a href="http://djlibrariandishes.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Denim-Jacket Librarian Dishes</a></i><br /><br />Who wouldn't want to rid themselves of any and all sickness or heal any injury the moment after it happens? To be free from such pitfalls as getting winded while running or healing muscles to help them grow stronger. It would sound like a good deal to most people. But for those with such abilities, like Ada, it is as much the dark side of the coin as it is the light especially when others want that skill for themselves alone. No one should be forced to do something against their will, and Ada refuses to let anyone, even her aunt who is also a healer, tell her how she should use her gift. <br /><br />At first I found it a little difficult to relate with Ada. Granted, she has been shuffled around foster homes for most of her life, her mother disappeared when she was little, and she has the bizarre skill of being able to "see others' sickness." That alone would probably make for a surly teenager. Still sometimes her negative venting became a bit tiresome though I have to admit that trait adds to her realistic nature.<br /><br />Ada also does a few things I thought were too risky given the situations she was in at the time, particularly when she was practicing her healing ability. I know practice helps boost improvement, but doing so in a public place among a group of people wasn't the smartest thing to do. I'll just chalk that up to her being a teenager and a novice when it comes to judgment. It was a nice change to see her assisting those who at least helped her even if that in itself was a risk.<br /><br />The supporting characters that were introduced once the story took Ada overseas were what really enabled her to grow as a person. She had been denied real kindness for so long in her life, it was great to see Ada treated so well even by people she had only just met. I really liked Madame Jardin and her willingness to give Ada a home in a strange country while she searched for her mother. McDonald even adds hints of romance into Ada with the introduction of Daniel, a young man who instructs Ada in parkour, free running. That was a unique touch as well since I haven't heard parkour used in another novel before, and McDonald was thinking outside the box with that addition.<br /><br />Overall, the pacing was nice and steady, and I felt really drawn into the story. There were some intense parts where I was on the edge of my seat while reading, and I have to say those parts added to the urgency I felt for Ada as she tried to stay one step ahead of those pursuing her as she searched for her mother. Now, I just have one question for R.A. McDonald: When will the next part of Ada's story be ready for we readers??? </span>
  <a data-text-id="12323232421948341848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_152346006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152346006" />
    <a title="Melissa (i swim for oceans)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3096138-melissa-i-swim-for-oceans"><img alt="Melissa (i swim for oceans)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274797276p2/3096138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152346006?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (i swim for oceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (i swim for oceans)" href="/user/show/3096138-melissa-i-swim-for-oceans">Melissa (i swim for oceans)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152346006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11799386733982321105">Ada's lived her entire life in the foster system, knowing she has a gift, but is convinced it's more of a curse than anything else. After pulling her last stunt and being caught, Ada is fifteen and past the age that people and her caseworker can simply overlook her childish rebellion. It's either time for her to stay in a home for kids that can't be placed in stable homes, or she goes to Aunt Jessie, her mother's best friend. The two share similar gifts, but Ada resents hers until her unique abi</span>
  <span id="freeText11799386733982321105" style="display:none">Ada's lived her entire life in the foster system, knowing she has a gift, but is convinced it's more of a curse than anything else. After pulling her last stunt and being caught, Ada is fifteen and past the age that people and her caseworker can simply overlook her childish rebellion. It's either time for her to stay in a home for kids that can't be placed in stable homes, or she goes to Aunt Jessie, her mother's best friend. The two share similar gifts, but Ada resents hers until her unique ability is brought to light and the extent of her power is revealed. Now her gift is a fight between life and death, and the life hanging in the balance is her own.<br /><br />I have to say this is a first for me. Healers in YA fiction is a nice, refreshing twist on magic and the paranormal, and it was truly a pleasure to lose myself in a world so vastly different than those I've seen. R.A. McDonald has created a world within Ada - Legend of a Healer that's dark and grim, all the while perfectly merging a delicate balance of human nature, the struggle to find oneself and a trippy world where Ada's gift has more than just the power to heal. With intricate details and clever artwork peppering the pages, Ada - Legend of a Healer was a rich world that one can easily lose themselves within.<br /><br />I didn't know what to expect from Ada, herself, when I started the book, but I was pleasantly surprised. Despite, or in spite of, her incredible gift, Ada is very much a normal teenager within Ada - Legend of a Healer. She's lived a difficult life outside of her gift, and her gift simply amplifies her struggle. Jessie was also a remarkable character. There were moments that I thought I knew her and loved her, and there were times I wanted to strangle her. Throughout it all though, it was apparent that she was doing the best she could, in her own way, to help Ada. The multiple settings, the search for Ada's mother, and the desperate desire to be someone Ada could come to terms with all made Ada - Legend of a Healer poignant and powerful. The only thing I would have specifically changed in the book was to have fleshed out the climax a bit more. I felt it was a bit rushed.<br /><br />It's rare that I come across a book that so pleasantly surprises me, especially when the cover isn't my favourite (I'm a cover slut...it's no secret). I give Ada - Legend of a Healer a very strong 4 out of 5, and I'd recommend it to the YA audience, particularly those who enjoy paranormal stories.<br /><br /><br />I received this book free of charge from the publisher in exchange for an honest review. This, in no way, affected my opinion or review of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11799386733982321105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_153940710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153940710?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki (Wicked Awesome Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki (Wicked Awesome Books)" href="/user/show/2833134-nikki-wicked-awesome-books">Nikki (Wicked Awesome Books)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2833134-nikki-wicked-awesome-books?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2833134-nikki-wicked-awesome-books?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2833134-nikki-wicked-awesome-books?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153940710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9018519597242596466">3.5<br/><br/>Ada Legend of a Healer is a compelling, interesting, and well-paced story that follows a 15 year old girl and her struggle with a power she never realized she possessed. Ada is young and jaded and it shows. She doesn’t trust people easily, including Jessie, the closest thing to family she has ever had. Her back and forth feelings regarding Jessie are a bit annoying, but easy to understand. Once Ada begins to accept her ‘gift’ more, she really grows and her morals develop a great deal.<br/><br/>The stor</span>
  <span id="freeText9018519597242596466" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />Ada Legend of a Healer is a compelling, interesting, and well-paced story that follows a 15 year old girl and her struggle with a power she never realized she possessed. Ada is young and jaded and it shows. She doesn’t trust people easily, including Jessie, the closest thing to family she has ever had. Her back and forth feelings regarding Jessie are a bit annoying, but easy to understand. Once Ada begins to accept her ‘gift’ more, she really grows and her morals develop a great deal.<br /><br />The story starts off a bit slow, but once it picks up, the pace moves swiftly and the story behind Ada’s mother’s disappearance really picks up. Ada’s insistence that the sick are sick and the hurt get hurt for a reason is a little sad, but I got it. She’s only one person and she doesn’t see how much of a difference she can make, and even if she should try to make a difference. Her life has been hard, without a family or a mother, but seeing her open up and let others in is worth it.<br /><br />Ada’s time in Paris is a nice change, both in setting and in her character. For a while, she’s happy. The kindness of strangers lets her loosen up and be young. Madame Jardin is the sweetest lady and Ada’s new Parkour buddies swept me off my feet. It’s an adrenaline rush to go along with Ada and Daniel as they run through the streets of Paris. Ada’s experiences with healing become more and more intense, but I would have liked to see more consequence to action. It doesn’t take anything out of Ada to heal, unless she’s fighting to stay conscious because of an injury. Aside from that, the healing is handled with care and I descriptions even seem realistic.<br /><br />Ada Legend of a Healer is an interesting take on a relatively common theme. The story is made that much more unique because of R.A. McDonald’s take on Ada’s gift and the dark illustrations scattered throughout. The story starts slow, but picks up quickly and leaves off with quite the cliffhanger. I sure hope a sequel is in the works because I’m ready to see where Ada’s story goes next.<br /><br />Opening line: Usually an indoor plant will bend and twist to find the direction with the most sun, but not the plant in Ada’s room. ~ pg. 1<br /><br />Favorite lines: “I know you know the difference between right and wrong. If someone slips and falls in front of you, would you help them up or just walk away?”<br /> “Depends on the person,” Ada retorted. ~ pg. 50</span>

<div id="review_171215661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171215661" />
    <a title="Marcie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3910792-marcie"><img alt="Marcie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293414073p2/3910792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171215661?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marcie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marcie" href="/user/show/3910792-marcie">Marcie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171215661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16375195090546893394">Ada is an interesting novel. The tagline to this book reads "If you had the power to heal, What would you do?" I thought that is a really interesting question. My first response to this question is yes, of course. Then after thinking about it for awhile, I began to reconsider my answer. There are many pros and cons that kept entering my mind. R.A. McDonald does a fantastic job answering these questions in Ada: Legend of a Healer. Ada is teenage girl who has grown up in foster care. She is not an</span>
  <span id="freeText16375195090546893394" style="display:none">Ada is an interesting novel. The tagline to this book reads "If you had the power to heal, What would you do?" I thought that is a really interesting question. My first response to this question is yes, of course. Then after thinking about it for awhile, I began to reconsider my answer. There are many pros and cons that kept entering my mind. R.A. McDonald does a fantastic job answering these questions in Ada: Legend of a Healer. Ada is teenage girl who has grown up in foster care. She is not an average teenager though, she has a special ability. Ada can not only sense sickness she can heal it. So far this gift has been a burden to her. It freaks people out if she tries to tell them. Because of this she is moved from one foster home to another over and over again. Ada has pretty much given up on humanity until she meets someone who can help unlock the mystery of who she is and what she can do. I thought the storyline in this book was outstanding. It's a bit dark at times but not without cause. It is a fast paced novel that keeps you on the edge of your seat. The setting of the book constantly changes as Ada tries to find answers to what happened to her mother. <br />Ada is a teenage girl that has been through a lot in her fifteen years of life. She's been moved around constantly. This leaves Ada disgruntled about life. She's rough around the edges but you can see bits and pieces of a softer side of her. Ada understandably has trust issues. She's always prepared to bolt if the need arises. I like her character a lot. McDonald does a great job of exposing Ada's insecurities and her strengths at the same time. Ada is forced to make tough decisions at a young age. Ada has to learn to trust. Through her journey she meets several interesting characters. My favorite character in this novel is Madame Jardin. She is an older lady that shows Ada true kindness.<br />Overall this was a really good book. It is a quick and easy read with a lot of depth to it. I enjoyed it from cover to cover. I'm not sure if this book is the first in a series but from the way it ended it could be. I would recommend this book to anyone that likes paranormal and is looking for something different to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16375195090546893394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162556409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162556409" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1361935-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310251400p2/1361935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162556409?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/1361935-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10758573-ada">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162556409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7293025181437026734">Ada is a very troubled young girl with a gift even she doesn't realize she has until her mother's friend fills her in. Ada has always been able to see other people's illnesses and maladies but didn't know that her touch could heal them. I'm not sure how you could make it 15 years before realizing that your touch heals people, but as I got the impression that none of her homes are particularly loving I suppose that she wasn't touching many people.<br/><br/><br/>I felt that McDonald got into the mind of a teenag</span>
  <span id="freeText7293025181437026734" style="display:none">Ada is a very troubled young girl with a gift even she doesn't realize she has until her mother's friend fills her in. Ada has always been able to see other people's illnesses and maladies but didn't know that her touch could heal them. I'm not sure how you could make it 15 years before realizing that your touch heals people, but as I got the impression that none of her homes are particularly loving I suppose that she wasn't touching many people.<br /><br /><br />I felt that McDonald got into the mind of a teenage girl fairly well. Especially a troubled teen. When Ada learns she can heal, her 'aunt' insists that they have an obligation to help people. In what I feel is fairly typical teenage behavior, Ada rebels against this idea. She's not about to do anything she doesn't want to do, be it out of obligation or force. It doesn't make her a bad person, in fact, most of the time she's willing to help out those around her without being asked but, being a teenager she just wants to feels as though she had a choice in the matter. <br /><br /><br />When Ada gets to Paris in an effort to find her long lost mother, she takes a small detour in her search to delve into the world of parkour after seeing a group of teenagers practicing this in an alley. At first I found it strange that after coming all this way and being so intent on finding her mother she would throw that aside to run around on building with a cute guy. The Ada I'd come to know up to that point wasn't the type to lose her focus over a guy so I found it strange. That is until she expressed a desire to learn so that she could always get away from the people who are hunting her in an effort to use her power for personal gain. Then it made a bit more sense. <br /><br /><br />All in all, despite not being my usual type of book, I found it to be an enjoyable YA story, accentuated by the artwork that is inserted randomly through the book. (It's been a minute since I read a book with pictures that wasn't geared towards my children.) In fact, as I read I kept thinking it was a book that my 13 year old niece and many other teens would likely enjoy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7293025181437026734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151958863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151958863" />
    <a title="Britney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2829197-britney"><img alt="Britney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464221565p2/2829197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151958863?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Britney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Britney" href="/user/show/2829197-britney">Britney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2829197-britney?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2829197-britney?shelf=2011-reading-list">2011-reading-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151958863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10527425666491058560">I'm going to be honest, I really am not a fan of this cover. I know it's wrong to judge a book by it's cover but I was still hesitant in reading this because of it. I'm so happy I got past my own first judgments because I really enjoyed this book. Within the book were also other drawings that fit scenes, which was different and interesting, but I still think I'd prefer a different cover. The book definitely needs some editing (a tad irksome but that might be because I'm an anal English major) bu</span>
  <span id="freeText10527425666491058560" style="display:none">I'm going to be honest, I really am not a fan of this cover. I know it's wrong to judge a book by it's cover but I was still hesitant in reading this because of it. I'm so happy I got past my own first judgments because I really enjoyed this book. Within the book were also other drawings that fit scenes, which was different and interesting, but I still think I'd prefer a different cover. The book definitely needs some editing (a tad irksome but that might be because I'm an anal English major) but even that didn't hinder my desire to keep reading.<br /><br />Ada, as you learn from the book description, has the power to heal people but she sees it more as a curse because of the situations she keeps finding herself in. She is on the run from the government and cruel doctors and a future with no freedom. But she also meets people she learns to care about after living her life distancing herself from foster families and ever-changing schools. And she learns more about herself and what she wants from her own life in the fast-paced and exciting journey she takes off on.<br /><br />I found Ada as a refreshingly strong female character. She was tough, resilient, and didn't need someone else to take care of her. And I loved that she could stick up for herself and was extremely loyal to those she loved and who loved her. She was the girl you'd want to become friends with, and not just because she could heal you from everything (from scraps and bruises to cancer).<br /><br />I also loved how I was always interested in what was happening. There was excitement and conflict and you were left exclaiming at the book or biting your nails. I was never left wondering "What was the point of that?" or feeling bored. There were so many great scenes and I loved rooting for Ada and feeling as though the story was in McDonald's capable hands. I think with a different cover and some editing this book could definitely sell itself.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ieatwords.com">www.ieatwords.com</a></span>

<div id="review_152535388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152535388" />
    <a title="Cynthia Larson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2263607-cynthia-larson"><img alt="Cynthia Larson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442451522p2/2263607.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152535388?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cynthia Larson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cynthia Larson" href="/user/show/2263607-cynthia-larson">Cynthia Larson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152535388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13000501187953192201"><b>Heroic Healer's Engaging Story</b><br/><br/>There's a lot to love in this fast-paced novel about a young teenage girl whose healing abilities provide her with both tremendous opportunities and challenges, as she embarks on a quest to track down her mother. Ada's journey has a sense of urgency to it, as she breaks free from her aunt's care to take off from Canada to France, keeping a low profile so as to not attract attention of those who seek to harness Ada's healing powers greedily for their own. While much </span>
  <span id="freeText13000501187953192201" style="display:none"><b>Heroic Healer's Engaging Story</b><br /><br />There's a lot to love in this fast-paced novel about a young teenage girl whose healing abilities provide her with both tremendous opportunities and challenges, as she embarks on a quest to track down her mother. Ada's journey has a sense of urgency to it, as she breaks free from her aunt's care to take off from Canada to France, keeping a low profile so as to not attract attention of those who seek to harness Ada's healing powers greedily for their own. While much of Ada's antisocial behavior at first seems a bit unusual, her history of having been moved from foster home to foster home help explain why she has learned to look after herself in a world where others seldom truly look after her. <br /><br />This book's interesting illustrations and simple vocabulary make it ideal for young readers who feel different than their peers. Ada is an empowering heroine who rises to meet any and all setbacks. Ada's avid interest and dedicated commitment to learning new skills set an excellent example of a young woman who is smart, strong, and compassionate. Many of Ada's deepest conflicts have to do with coming to terms with how she sees herself in relation to others in the world, as she frequently wonders about just how responsible she ought to be when blessed as she is with the power to heal anyone of any ailment. <br /><br />I know a book is wonderful when I read it straight through, and have trouble putting it down, and Ada: Legend of a Healer is a page-turner! This book deeply touches my heart, as it addresses feelings that a young woman would have of wondering how best to fit into a world full of people who would seek to possess or control those who have gifts to heal. This story has such a strong ring of truth to it that I frequently found myself feeling that this is a true story about a girl I'd really love to meet. <br /><br />Highly recommended for readers of all ages!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13000501187953192201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_152307469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152307469" />
    <a title="Amanda-Lee (StoryWings)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2888182-amanda-lee-storywings"><img alt="Amanda-Lee (StoryWings)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294567899p2/2888182.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152307469?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda-Lee (StoryWings)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda-Lee (StoryWings)" href="/user/show/2888182-amanda-lee-storywings">Amanda-Lee (StoryWings)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2888182-amanda-lee-storywings?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2888182-amanda-lee-storywings?shelf=review-book">review-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152307469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11554645982399177346">Ada Legend of a Healer had a bad start, but ended up turning into a rather good read.<br/><br/>Ada is an orphan with an attitude problem. After getting kicked out of yet another foster home she can’t be placed anywhere else, so she leaves the system, embarking on her own journey to find her mother. Her journey leads her to France and the people she meets there help her hone not only her healing skills but develop skills in the art of parkour.<br/><br/>Ada was not a likeable character for most of the story. Her only</span>
  <span id="freeText11554645982399177346" style="display:none">Ada Legend of a Healer had a bad start, but ended up turning into a rather good read.<br /><br />Ada is an orphan with an attitude problem. After getting kicked out of yet another foster home she can’t be placed anywhere else, so she leaves the system, embarking on her own journey to find her mother. Her journey leads her to France and the people she meets there help her hone not only her healing skills but develop skills in the art of parkour.<br /><br />Ada was not a likeable character for most of the story. Her only redeeming attribute was her sheer force of will power, all of her other aspects boiled down to her being an egotistical, self-centred teenager. For the first hundred pages I had the urge to not only scream but stick a fork in my eye because of the constant whining about how unfair the world is and how unfair it is that she have to bear the burden of having the ability to heal not only others, but herself.<br /><br /><br />Ada Legend of a Healer did start to get interesting when Ada went to France on her mission to find her mother. After using Jessie – her aunt – for money and information Ada struck out on her own to find out if her mother was still alive.<br /><br />Delving into the world of parkour and the limits of Ada’s power was the highlight of the novel because we got to see McDonalds writing ability on show. Daniel and his friends and Daniel’s budding romance with Ada drove the novel from that point.<br /><br /><br />Ada Legend of a Healer was a slow read to get started and once it got going it was easy to see where it would end up, but I felt oddly compelled to finish, quickly. McDonalds writing drew me in after Ada got to France to a point where I couldn’t let go and Ada’s story wouldn’t let me go. Even after the final page was turned McDonalds message - to cherish what you have - stayed with me for a long time afterwards.<br /><br />Find this review at storywings.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="11554645982399177346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150073122?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaisa" href="/user/show/3017954-kaisa">Kaisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150073122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7243845343067882363">Clarification: 3,5/5 stars.<br/><br/>This book was incredibly creative and fun to read. It's been a while since I've read a book with illustrations. I just love the artwork. To me, it added something extra, something that was needed to make this story stand out.<br/>Does that mean I didn't like the story?<br/><br/>No it does not.<br/><br/>I liked the story. It had a girl with a troubled past, who could heal herself (and others, of course), a crazy senator who wanted to use her powers for selfish reasons.... parkour!!.... in Franc</span>
  <span id="freeText7243845343067882363" style="display:none">Clarification: 3,5/5 stars.<br /><br />This book was incredibly creative and fun to read. It's been a while since I've read a book with illustrations. I just love the artwork. To me, it added something extra, something that was needed to make this story stand out.<br />Does that mean I didn't like the story?<br /><br />No it does not.<br /><br />I liked the story. It had a girl with a troubled past, who could heal herself (and others, of course), a crazy senator who wanted to use her powers for selfish reasons.... parkour!!.... in France!.. with french people!! So yeah, to say that it had loads of potential is an understatement. But somehow it didn't live up to it. At least not fully. <br />It felt like the text kept scratching at the surface of what could be an awesome book. I wanted more time with the different characters, I wanted a scary senator that I wouldn't forget so easily and I wanted Ada's powers to be more mysterious. As it was, she went around revealing it to everyone she met.<br /> <br />But yes, I did like it. I especially liked-- no, loved --the main character. At least in the first part of the book. She was very refreshing and feisty, definitely not as forgettable as a lot of other females in YA literature. I liked how she didn't want to heal the world. I liked how her troubled past truly affected her personality. <br />Main characters don't have to be all-caring and wonderful to be sympathetic and interesting to us readers, people. Let's not forget that.<br /><br />Anyway, the story isn't over! Or so the last page told me.<br />This makes me happy, because maybe, just maybe, I'll get that depth I was hoping to get in the sequel(s?).<br /><br />Do I recommend it?<br />Yes I do.<br /><br />And to repeat myself: I loved the artwork. And the butterflies. Very grungy and personal. Unique.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7243845343067882363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_156212687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156212687" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156212687?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10758573-ada">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156212687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15218382640130976943">A Compleat Pleasure<br/><br/>R.A. McDonald certainly knows her away around the maze within the minds of teenagers: few writers can match her gifts at expressing the angst and frustrations of 'lost kids' and still manage to deal with the adult characters around them in a three-dimensional manner that creates a solid atmosphere for compelling story telling. What's more she has the courage to blend her story with 'illustrations' (by a fine artist by the name of James McDonald) to create a new approach to boo</span>
  <span id="freeText15218382640130976943" style="display:none">A Compleat Pleasure<br /><br />R.A. McDonald certainly knows her away around the maze within the minds of teenagers: few writers can match her gifts at expressing the angst and frustrations of 'lost kids' and still manage to deal with the adult characters around them in a three-dimensional manner that creates a solid atmosphere for compelling story telling. What's more she has the courage to blend her story with 'illustrations' (by a fine artist by the name of James McDonald) to create a new approach to books - this is not a graphic novel nor is it a child's book with occasional 'pictures'. This book is an art book that marries a griping story with atmospheric art that hopefully will become an idea the author will continue in what most assuredly will be followup books both about the characters in this novel and other books that are likely already germinating in her pregnant mind. <br /><br />Ada is an orphan, in her teens, bouncing form foster home to foster home because of her apparent antisocial acting out. Social workers finally contact her Aunt Jessie, a peculiar mysterious but warm woman who takes Ada into her confidence that she is a healer. Jessie informs Ada that Ada's mother is living in Paris, helps Ada 'discover' her abilities as a healer, then warns Ada about a Senator who will prey on her to assure he maintains the fountain of youth. With Jessie's goodwill and supervision Ada makes it to Paris to find the mother she never knew and the secrets that surround her mother's life - and her own. Along the way Ada metamorphoses from an antisocial troubled teen to a sensitive and compassionate healer. And the manner in which this happens is, in McDonald's hands, a fine story of coming of age and appreciating priorities in a life altered by extra-human powers. <br /><br />Grady Harp</span>
  <a data-text-id="15218382640130976943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SLlQBunUG5dTlQQdowLOyh6RuiPSy878gWXB0kyLhAYnDki+C7PGFMkoT2RLZ3sghM/pha/DV0NFa8icoJ1u8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Pg4S/c8c8n8FUPCZXPGwYl3iZEYEJfute+5TcTzDANtRuQpFLXsv/J/tu+C0lAWIx7w34HktYhK/4Fo/0NXqLQ==')})
  }
